## Problem

Suppose $\Omega$ and $\Gamma$ intersect at two distinct points $A$ and $B$. Line $MN$ intersects $\Omega$ at $C$ and $\Gamma$ at $D$, so that $C, M, N, D$ lie on $MN$ in that order. However there is a risk that the algebra becomes too messy. But we can try to simplify using vector methods and some known formulas. Let's attempt.

Set M = (0,0), N = (1,0). Then:

C = (-r1, 0)
D = (1 + r2, 0)

A = (x0, y0) with

x0 = (1 + r1^2 - r2^2) / 2
y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2

Simplify y0^2:

y0^2 = r1^2 - ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2 / 4) = (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

We'll keep it as is.

Now P = circumcenter of ACD. Since C and D are on x-axis, we already found x_P = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( -r1 + (1 + r2) )/2 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2. So x_P is that. Then y_P is determined by equality of distances to A and C. Let's compute y_P explicitly.

We have:

|P C|^2 = (x_P - (-r1))^2 + y_P^2 = (x_P + r1)^2 + y_P^2.
|P A|^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + (y_P - y0)^2.

Set equal:

(x_P + r1)^2 + y_P^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + (y_P - y0)^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + y_P^2 - 2 y_P y0 + y0^2.

Cancel y_P^2:

(x_P + r1)^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 - 2 y_P y0 + y0^2.

Thus 2 y_P y0 = (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2.

So y_P = [ (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2 ] / (2 y0).

Now compute (x_P - x0)^2 and (x_P + r1)^2. We have:

x_P + r1 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2 + r1 = (1 + r2 - r1 + 2 r1)/2 = (1 + r2 + r1)/2. Good.

x_P - x0 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)/2 = ( (1 + r2 - r1) - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2) )/2 = ( r2 - r1 - r1^2 + r2^2 )/2.

We can simplify numerator: (r2^2 - r1^2) + (r2 - r1) = (r2 - r1)(r2 + r1) + (r2 - r1) = (r2 - r1)(r2 + r1 + 1). So:

x_P - x0 = ( (r2 - r1)(r1 + r2 + 1) ) / 2.

Thus (x_P - x0)^2 = ((r2 - r1)^2 (r1 + r2 + 1)^2) / 4.

Now (x_P + r1)^2 = ((1 + r1 + r2)^2) / 4.

So numerator:

N = (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2 = (1/4)[(r2 - r1)^2 (r1 + r2 + 1)^2 - (1 + r1 + r2)^2] + y0^2.

Simplify the bracket. Let S = r1 + r2. Then (r2 - r1)^2 (S+1)^2 - (S+1)^2 = (S+1)^2[ (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 ].

But is that correct? (1 + r1 + r2) = S+1. So we have:

((r2 - r1)^2 (S+1)^2 - (S+1)^2 = (S+1)^2[ (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 ].

Thus:

N = (1/4)(S+1)^2[ (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 ] + y0^2.

Now we need y0^2 expressed in terms of r1,r2. Recall y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2. x0 = (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)/2. So compute x0^2. Let's do systematically.

Set d=1. Then:

x0 = (d^2 - r2^2 + r1^2) / (2d) = (1 - r2^2 + r1^2) / 2.
y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2.

Compute x0^2:

x0^2 = ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Thus y0^2 = r1^2 - ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4 = (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Now we also have (r2 - r1)^2 = r1^2 + r2^2 - 2 r1 r2. And (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 = (r1^2 + r2^2 - 2 r1 r2) - 1.

Thus N becomes:

N = (1/4)(S+1)^2 * ((r2 - r1)^2 - 1) + (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Factor 1/4: N = 1/4 [ (S+1)^2 * ((r2 - r1)^2 - 1) + (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) ].

We can attempt to simplify this expression. But maybe we don't need explicit y_P. Instead, we can find H and then compute the line L and then check tangency with (BEF). But maybe there is a synthetic insight that avoids heavy algebra.

|O - B|^2 = |O - E|^2  вҶ’ (O - B)В·(O - B) = (O - E)В·(O - E) вҶ’ -2 OВ·B + |B|^2 = -2 OВ·E + |E|^2 вҶ’ 2 OВ·(E - B) = |E|^2 - |B|^2.

Similarly, |O - B|^2 = |O - F|^2 вҶ’ 2 OВ·(F - B) = |F|^2 - |B|^2.

So we have two linear equations in O. That's manageable. So we can solve for O as a point (vector) in terms of B,E,F. Then compute radius squared R^2 = |O - B|^2. Then compute distance from O to line L (through H with direction v) and compare.

But we need to prove tangency, which is equivalent to: (distance from O to L)^2 = R^2.

So we can compute that.

But we also have expressions for Оұ and ОІ, and we know B, a, v. Maybe the algebra simplifies nicely. Let's try to compute O.

Also note that we have P = a + v. So |v|^2 = |P - A|^2.

Now we also have linear relation: PВ·A = -r1 X. But maybe we can find expressions for |a|^2, |b|^2, |e|^2, |f|^2.

We know |a|^2 = r1^2. |b|^2 = |a|^2 = r1^2 (since reflection across axis). So |B|^2 = r1^2.

Now |e|^2 = |a + Оұ v|^2 = |a|^2 + 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 |v|^2. But aВ·v = AВ·(P - A) = AВ·P - |a|^2 = -r1 X - r1^2 = -r1 (X + r1). So aВ·v = -r1 (X + r1). That's negative. Then |e|^2 = r1^2 - 2Оұ r1 (X + r1) + Оұ^2 R^2.

Similarly, |f|^2 = r1^2 - 2ОІ r1 (X + r1) + ОІ^2 R^2.

Now also we can compute Оұ and ОІ in terms of R^2 and S. So we can substitute.

We have Оұ = r1 S / R^2, ОІ = r2 S / R^2. Then Оұ R^2 = r1 S. Similarly ОІ R^2 = r2 S.

Now compute |e|^2 = r1^2 - 2 r1 (X + r1) * (Оұ) + Оұ^2 R^2 = r1^2 - 2 r1 (X + r1) * (r1 S / R^2) + (r1^2 S^2 / R^4) * R^2 = r1^2 - 2 r1^2 (X + r1) S / R^2 + (r1^2 S^2) / R^2.

Simplify: |e|^2 = r1^2 + \frac{r1^2}{R^2} \left( -2 (X + r1) S + S^2 \right).

Similarly, |f|^2 = r1^2 + \frac{r1^2}{R^2} \left( -2 (X + r1) S + S^2 \right) but with r2? Actually careful: |f|^2 = r1^2 - 2ОІ r1 (X + r1) + ОІ^2 R^2. Substitute ОІ = r2 S / R^2. So |f|^2 = r1^2 + \frac{1}{R^2} \left( -2 r1 r2 S (X + r1) + r2^2 S^2 \right).

That seems different from |e|^2. So we have two different expressions. But maybe we can simplify further using relationships between X, r1, r2, S. We'll need to compute O.

Now, AВ·v = AВ·(P - A) = AВ·P - r1^2. And we know AВ·P = -r1 X, so AВ·v = -r1 X - r1^2 = -r1 (X + r1). Also, X + r1 = S/2. So AВ·v = -r1 * (S/2) = -r1 S / 2.

Thus:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) * ( - r1 S / 2 ) + (ОІ - Оұ) (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) ( - r1 S ) + (ОІ - Оұ) (ОІ + Оұ) R^2.

Now, ОІ - Оұ = (r2 - r1) S / R^2. So:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = ( (r2 - r1) S / R^2 ) * ( - r1 S ) + ( (r2 - r1) S / R^2 ) * (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = - (r1 (r2 - r1) S^2) / R^2 + (r2 - r1) S * (ОІ + Оұ).

Now, (ОІ + Оұ) = (r2 + r1) S / R^2. So (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (r1 + r2) S. Then

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = - (r1 (r2 - r1) S^2 / R^2 + (r2 - r1) S * ( (r1 + r2) S / R^2 )? Wait careful: (ОІ + Оұ) S? Actually we have (ОІ - Оұ) S * (ОІ + Оұ) R^2? Let's recompute:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) * (- r1 S) + (ОІ - Оұ) * (ОІ + Оұ) * R^2? Actually we have (ОІ^2 - Оұ^2) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ)(ОІ + Оұ) R^2. So

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) AВ·v + (ОІ - Оұ)(ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) [ 2 AВ·v + (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 ].

But we also derived an expression earlier that gave |E|^2 - |F|^2 = - S^2 r2 (r2 - r1) / R^2. That seemed to be derived from the expansions with Оұ and ОІ. Let's verify that derivation.

We had:

|E|^2 - r1^2 = 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2.
|F|^2 - r1^2 = 2ОІ aВ·v + ОІ^2 R^2.

But we also have from (1) that 4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2. That's not directly about |E|^2 - r1^2, but we can compute |E|^2 - r1^2 using param. That's simpler. So |E|^2 - r1^2 = 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2. Since |E|^2 = r1^2, that's zero. So 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = 0. That gives a relation: Оұ (2 aВ·v + Оұ R^2) = 0 вҶ’ Since Оұ>0, we have 2 aВ·v + Оұ R^2 = 0 вҶ’ aВ·v = -Оұ R^2 / 2. But we also have aВ·v = -r1 S / 2. And Оұ R^2 = r1 S. So -Оұ R^2 / 2 = -r1 S / 2, which matches aВ·v. So that's consistent. So indeed |E|^2 - r1^2 = 0 gives 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = 0. That's an equation that relates aВ·v and Оұ, R^2. Since we have Оұ R^2 = r1 S, that's automatically satisfied. So that's not a new relation.

Now, the expression we derived for |E|^2 - |F|^2 using the param gave - S^2 r2 (r2 - r1) / R^2. But we need to double-check that calculation because earlier we used expressions for |E|^2 - r1^2 and |F|^2 - r1^2 in terms of S, R^2, X, etc. That might have been erroneous. Let's recompute carefully with the param.

Define:

a = A, v = P - a. Then R^2 = |v|^2.

Оұ = r1 S / R^2, ОІ = r2 S / R^2.

Then:

Thus |F|^2 = r1^2 + \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{R^2}.

Simplify y0^2:

y0^2 = r1^2 - ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2 / 4) = (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

We'll keep it as is.

Now P = circumcenter of ACD. Since C and D are on x-axis, we already found x_P = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( -r1 + (1 + r2) )/2 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2. So x_P is that. Then y_P is determined by equality of distances to A and C. Let's compute y_P explicitly.

We have:

|P C|^2 = (x_P - (-r1))^2 + y_P^2 = (x_P + r1)^2 + y_P^2.
|P A|^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + (y_P - y0)^2.

Set equal:

(x_P + r1)^2 + y_P^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + (y_P - y0)^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 + y_P^2 - 2 y_P y0 + y0^2.

Cancel y_P^2:

(x_P + r1)^2 = (x_P - x0)^2 - 2 y_P y0 + y0^2.

Thus 2 y_P y0 = (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2.

So y_P = [ (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2 ] / (2 y0).

Now compute (x_P - x0)^2 and (x_P + r1)^2. We have:

x_P + r1 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2 + r1 = (1 + r2 - r1 + 2 r1)/2 = (1 + r2 + r1)/2. Good.

x_P - x0 = (1 + r2 - r1)/2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)/2 = ( (1 + r2 - r1) - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2) )/2 = ( r2 - r1 - r1^2 + r2^2 )/2.

We can simplify numerator: (r2^2 - r1^2) + (r2 - r1) = (r2 - r1)(r2 + r1) + (r2 - r1) = (r2 - r1)(r2 + r1 + 1). So:

x_P - x0 = ( (r2 - r1)(r1 + r2 + 1) ) / 2.

Thus (x_P - x0)^2 = ((r2 - r1)^2 (r1 + r2 + 1)^2) / 4.

Now (x_P + r1)^2 = ((1 + r1 + r2)^2) / 4.

So numerator:

N = (x_P - x0)^2 + y0^2 - (x_P + r1)^2 = (1/4)[(r2 - r1)^2 (r1 + r2 + 1)^2 - (1 + r1 + r2)^2] + y0^2.

But is that correct? (1 + r1 + r2) = S+1. So we have:

((r2 - r1)^2 (S+1)^2 - (S+1)^2 = (S+1)^2[ (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 ].

Thus:

N = (1/4)(S+1)^2[ (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 ] + y0^2.

Now we need y0^2 expressed in terms of r1,r2. Recall y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2. x0 = (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)/2. So compute x0^2. Let's do systematically.

Set d=1. Then:

x0 = (d^2 - r2^2 + r1^2) / (2d) = (1 - r2^2 + r1^2) / 2.
y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2.

Compute x0^2:

x0^2 = ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Thus y0^2 = r1^2 - ((1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4 = (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Now we also have (r2 - r1)^2 = r1^2 + r2^2 - 2 r1 r2. And (r2 - r1)^2 - 1 = (r1^2 + r2^2 - 2 r1 r2) - 1.

Thus N becomes:

N = (1/4)(S+1)^2 * ((r2 - r1)^2 - 1) + (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) / 4.

Factor 1/4: N = 1/4 [ (S+1)^2 * ((r2 - r1)^2 - 1) + (4 r1^2 - (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2) ].

We have (P - A)^2 = (P - C)^2 вҶ’ expand: |P|^2 - 2 PВ·A + |A|^2 = |P|^2 - 2 PВ·C + |C|^2 вҶ’ Cancel |P|^2 вҶ’ -2 PВ·A + |A|^2 = -2 PВ·C + |C|^2 вҶ’ 2 PВ·(C - A) = |C|^2 - |A|^2. That's a linear equation in P (dot product). So indeed it's linear. So we can solve for y_P given x_P. Good.

Thus we can compute y_P easily. Let's do that.

Let P = (x_P, y_P). Then:

2 PВ·(C - A) = |C|^2 - |A|^2.

Compute C - A = (-r1 - x0, 0 - y0) = ( -r1 - x0, -y0). Then PВ·(C - A) = x_P (-r1 - x0) + y_P (-y0) = -x_P (r1 + x0) - y_P y0.

Thus 2 [ -x_P (r1 + x0) - y_P y0 ] = |C|^2 - |A|^2.

|C|^2 = (-r1)^2 + 0^2 = r1^2.
|A|^2 = r1^2 (since A lies on О©). So |C|^2 - |A|^2 = 0. That's interesting! Since both A and C lie on О© (circle centered at M), we have |A - M|^2 = r1^2, and |C - M|^2 = r1^2. 2 [ -x_P (r1 + x0) - y_P y0 ] = 0 вҶ’ -x_P (r1 + x0) - y_P y0 = 0 вҶ’ y_P y0 = -x_P (r1 + x0). (Equation 1)

That is a linear condition linking P and A. Good.

2 OВ·(F - B) = |F|^2 - r1^2 вҶ’ 4 y0 O_y + 2ОІ u = |F|^2 - r1^2.

Subtract the first from the second: 2 (ОІ - Оұ) u = |F|^2 - r1^2. That's exactly (III). So that's fine.

Now, what about the expression we derived earlier for u using |E|^2 - |F|^2? That came from considering the two equations after expanding with Оұ and ОІ, but then we set up something like 2 w + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2, etc. That was using w = OВ·(0,2 y0). Let's re-evaluate that step carefully.

We had:

OВ·(E - B) = 0 вҶ’ OВ·( (0,2 y0) + Оұ v ) = 2 y0 O_y + Оұ u = 0. That's one equation.

OВ·(F - B) = (|F|^2 - r1^2)/2 вҶ’ 2 y0 O_y + ОІ u = (|F|^2 - r1^2)/2.

So indeed we have two equations. That's what we used. So the earlier derivation of u from |E|^2 - |F|^2 was based on a different expansion (maybe with 2 OВ·(E - B) and 2 OВ·(F - B)). Let's confirm: 

2 OВ·(E - B) = 2 (2 y0 O_y + Оұ u) = 4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u. That's what we have. So equation (1) is 4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2. But we also know that |E|^2 = r1^2, so RHS=0. That's consistent. Similarly for F. So we have:

4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u = 0.   (1)
4 y0 O_y + 2ОІ u = |F|^2 - r1^2.   (2)

Now, if we subtract (1) from (2), we get 2 (ОІ - Оұ) u = |F|^2 - r1^2. That's one equation. That's what we have. So u is expressed in terms of |F|^2 - r1^2. That seems less direct. However earlier I derived u = S r2 / 2 using the expressions for |E|^2 - r1^2 and |F|^2 - r1^2 in terms of Оұ and ОІ, but that derivation used the equations 2 w + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2 and 2 w + 2ОІ u = |F|^2 - r1^2, where w = OВ·(0,2 y0). But note that 2 w = 2 * (2 y0 O_y) = 4 y0 O_y. So that's exactly the same. So the equations we have are:

4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2.
4 y0 O_y + 2ОІ u = |F|^2 - r1^2.

Then subtract: 2 (ОІ - Оұ) u = |F|^2 - |E|^2. That's another relation. That's valid. So we have both:

2 (ОІ - Оұ) u = |F|^2 - |E|^2.   (A)
2 (ОІ - Оұ) u = |F|^2 - r1^2 - (|E|^2 - r1^2) = |F|^2 - |E|^2. Yes, that's the same.

But earlier we computed |F|^2 - |E|^2 using the param. Let's compute that directly.

We have:

E = A + Оұ v, F = A + ОІ v. Then |E|^2 = |A|^2 + 2Оұ AВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = r1^2 + 2Оұ AВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2.
Similarly, |F|^2 = r1^2 + 2ОІ AВ·v + ОІ^2 R^2.
Thus |F|^2 - |E|^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) AВ·v + (ОІ^2 - Оұ^2) R^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) AВ·v + (ОІ - Оұ)(ОІ + Оұ) R^2.

Now, AВ·v = AВ·(P - A) = AВ·P - r1^2. And we know AВ·P = -r1 X, so AВ·v = -r1 X - r1^2 = -r1 (X + r1). Also, X + r1 = S/2. So AВ·v = -r1 * (S/2) = -r1 S / 2.

Thus:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) * ( - r1 S / 2 ) + (ОІ - Оұ) (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) ( - r1 S ) + (ОІ - Оұ) (ОІ + Оұ) R^2.

Now, ОІ - Оұ = (r2 - r1) S / R^2. So:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = ( (r2 - r1) S / R^2 ) * ( - r1 S ) + ( (r2 - r1) S / R^2 ) * (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = - (r1 (r2 - r1) S^2) / R^2 + (r2 - r1) S * (ОІ + Оұ).

Now, (ОІ + Оұ) = (r2 + r1) S / R^2. So (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (r1 + r2) S. Then

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = - (r1 (r2 - r1) S^2 / R^2 + (r2 - r1) S * ( (r1 + r2) S / R^2 )? Wait careful: (ОІ + Оұ) S? Actually we have (ОІ - Оұ) S * (ОІ + Оұ) R^2? Let's recompute:

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) * (- r1 S) + (ОІ - Оұ) * (ОІ + Оұ) * R^2? Actually we have (ОІ^2 - Оұ^2) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ)(ОІ + Оұ) R^2. So

|F|^2 - |E|^2 = 2 (ОІ - Оұ) AВ·v + (ОІ - Оұ)(ОІ + Оұ) R^2 = (ОІ - Оұ) [ 2 AВ·v + (ОІ + Оұ) R^2 ].

But we also derived an expression earlier that gave |E|^2 - |F|^2 = - S^2 r2 (r2 - r1) / R^2. That seemed to be derived from the expansions with Оұ and ОІ. Let's verify that derivation.

We had:

|E|^2 - r1^2 = 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2.
|F|^2 - r1^2 = 2ОІ aВ·v + ОІ^2 R^2.

But we also have from (1) that 4 y0 O_y + 2Оұ u = |E|^2 - r1^2. That's not directly about |E|^2 - r1^2, but we can compute |E|^2 - r1^2 using param. That's simpler. So |E|^2 - r1^2 = 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2. Since |E|^2 = r1^2, that's zero. So 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = 0. That gives a relation: Оұ (2 aВ·v + Оұ R^2) = 0 вҶ’ Since Оұ>0, we have 2 aВ·v + Оұ R^2 = 0 вҶ’ aВ·v = -Оұ R^2 / 2. But we also have aВ·v = -r1 S / 2. And Оұ R^2 = r1 S. So -Оұ R^2 / 2 = -r1 S / 2, which matches aВ·v. So that's consistent. So indeed |E|^2 - r1^2 = 0 gives 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = 0. That's an equation that relates aВ·v and Оұ, R^2. Since we have Оұ R^2 = r1 S, that's automatically satisfied. So that's not a new relation.

Now, the expression we derived for |E|^2 - |F|^2 using the param gave - S^2 r2 (r2 - r1) / R^2. But we need to double-check that calculation because earlier we used expressions for |E|^2 - r1^2 and |F|^2 - r1^2 in terms of S, R^2, X, etc. That might have been erroneous. Let's recompute carefully with the param.

Define:

a = A, v = P - a. Then R^2 = |v|^2.

Оұ = r1 S / R^2, ОІ = r2 S / R^2.

Then:

E = a + Оұ v. Then |E|^2 = |a|^2 + 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = r1^2 + 2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2. Since |E|^2 = r1^2 (by definition), we get:

2Оұ aВ·v + Оұ^2 R^2 = 0.   (1)

Similarly, F = a + ОІ v. Then |F|^2 = r1^2 + 2ОІ aВ·v + ОІ^2 R^2. But we know |F - N|^2 = r2^2, not |F|^2. So |F|^2 is not necessarily r1^2. So (1) is a relation that holds for E. It gives:

aВ·v = -Оұ R^2 / 2.   (1')

Now compute |F|^2 - r1^2 = 2ОІ aВ·v + ОІ^2 R^2. Substitute aВ·v = -r1 S / 2. Then:

|F|^2 - r1^2 = 2ОІ * (-r1 S / 2) + ОІ^2 R^2 = -ОІ r1 S + ОІ^2 R^2.

Now ОІ = r2 S / R^2. So ОІ^2 R^2 = (r2^2 S^2 / R^4) * R^2 = r2^2 S^2 / R^2. Also ОІ r1 S = (r2 S / R^2) * r1 S = r1 r2 S^2 / R^2. Thus

|F|^2 - r1^2 = - r1 r2 S^2 / R^2 + r2^2 S^2 / R^2 = \frac{S^2}{R^2} ( r2^2 - r1 r2 ) = \frac{S^2}{R^2} r2 ( r2 - r1 ). So

|F|^2 - r1^2 = \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{R^2}.   (2)

Thus |F|^2 = r1^2 + \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{R^2}.

Now, |F|^2 - r1^2 is positive, as expected.

4 y0 O_y + 2ОІ u = |F|^2 - r1^2.   (II)

Thus u = S r2 / 2. Good. That's consistent.

X (r1 + x0) = \frac{ S (1 - (r2 - r1)^2) }{4}.

Thus p = -X (r1 + x0) / y0 = - \frac{ S (1 - (r2 - r1)^2) }{4 y0 }.

Wx Ox + Wy Oy = K.

We can solve for Ox, Oy. That's straightforward.

Now, Ux = Оұ vx, Uy = 2 y0 + Оұ vy.
Wx = ОІ vx, Wy = 2 y0 + ОІ vy.

ОІ vx Ox + (2 y0 + ОІ vy) Oy = K.   (2)

We know K = (|F|^2 - r1^2)/2 = \frac{ S^2 r2 (r2 - r1) }{2 R^2 }? Actually |F|^2 - r1^2 = \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{R^2}. So K = \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{2 R^2}.

Now, we can solve for Ox and Oy. This seems more direct because we have explicit coefficients. Let's attempt.

From (1): Оұ vx Ox = - (2 y0 + Оұ vy) Oy вҶ’ Ox = - \frac{ (2 y0 + Оұ vy) }{ Оұ vx } Oy.   (A)

Plug into (2):

ОІ vx * ( - \frac{ (2 y0 + Оұ vy) }{ Оұ vx } Oy ) + (2 y0 + ОІ vy) Oy = K вҶ’ - \frac{ ОІ }{ Оұ } (2 y0 + Оұ vy) Oy + (2 y0 + ОІ vy) Oy = K вҶ’ Oy * [ - \frac{ ОІ }{ Оұ } (2 y0 + Оұ vy) + (2 y0 + ОІ vy) ] = K.

Simplify the bracket:

- \frac{ ОІ }{ Оұ } (2 y0 + Оұ vy) + (2 y0 + ОІ vy) = - \frac{ ОІ }{ Оұ } * 2 y0 - \frac{ ОІ }{ Оұ } * Оұ vy + 2 y0 + ОІ vy = - \frac{2 ОІ y0}{Оұ} - ОІ vy + 2 y0 + ОІ vy = 2 y0 (1 - \frac{ОІ}{Оұ}) + ( -ОІ vy + ОІ vy ) = 2 y0 (1 - \frac{ОІ}{Оұ}).

So we get:

Oy * 2 y0 (1 - \frac{ОІ}{Оұ}) = K.

Thus

Oy = \frac{ K }{ 2 y0 (1 - \frac{ОІ}{Оұ}) }.

Now, Оұ and ОІ are given. Since Оұ = r1 S / R^2, ОІ = r2 S / R^2, so ОІ/Оұ = r2 / r1. Thus 1 - ОІ/Оұ = 1 - r2/r1 = (r1 - r2)/r1 = - (r2 - r1)/r1 = - a / r1.

Thus 1 - ОІ/Оұ = - a / r1.

Then

Oy = \frac{ K }{ 2 y0 * ( - a / r1 ) } = \frac{ K * r1 }{ -2 a y0 } = - \frac{ r1 K }{ 2 a y0 }.

Now, K = \frac{S^2 r2 (r2 - r1)}{2 R^2} = \frac{S^2 r2 a}{2 R^2}.

Thus

Let's try to compute O_x using the linear system solution we already have. O_x = \frac{ u (2 y0 + Оұ vy) }{ 2 y0 vx }? Actually we derived O_x from the linear system as O_x = \frac{ Uy K R^2 }{ a^2 S^2 y0 }. But maybe we can also find O_x using the equation OВ·v = u. That gave O_x = (u - O_y vy) / vx. That's fine. Let's compute O_x with that.

We have O_y = - \frac{ 4 r1 r2 y0 }{ 4 y0^2 + (1 - a^2)^2 }. vy is known. Then O_x = (u - O_y vy) / vx. This seems messy. However we can also compute O_x using the formula for the circumcenter of an isosceles triangle. Since BE = EF, the triangle is isosceles with vertex at E. Then the circumcenter lies on the line that is the perpendicular bisector of BF, which passes through E. So O is somewhere on that line. That line has direction perpendicular to BF. So O can be expressed as O = E + О» * n, where n is a unit vector perpendicular to BF. Also, O is equidistant to E and B, but that's automatically satisfied if O lies on perpendicular bisector of BF? Actually O lies on perpendicular bisector of BF, so O is equidistant to B and F. But also O must be equidistant to E and B. Since BE = EF, the perpendicular bisector of BF passes through E, but that doesn't guarantee that O is equidistant to E and B. However for the circumcenter O of triangle BEF, we have |O - B| = |O - E| = |O - F|. So O is equidistant to B and E, and also to B and F. So O lies on perpendicular bisector of BE and BF. Since BE = EF, the perpendicular bisector of BE is not obviously related. But we can use that O lies on perpendicular bisector of BF. So O is on the line through E perpendicular to BF. So we can set O = E + Ој * (BF)^\perp. That's one equation. Also, O lies on perpendicular bisector of EF. That's another line. So O is the intersection. So we have two lines. That might be easier to solve than the linear system. Let's attempt to compute O using that approach.

We have E = A + v (since Оұ=1). So E is P (since Оұ=1). That's a nice simplification! Indeed, Оұ = r1 S / R^2, and we earlier observed that Оұ = 1? No, Оұ is not generally 1. In the numeric examples, Оұ turned out to be 1 because r1 S / R^2 = 1. That happened when R^2 = r1 S. But is that always true? Let's compute R^2 = |v|^2. We have v = P - A. We know that PВ·A = -r1 X, and |A|^2 = r1^2. So |v|^2 = |P - A|^2 = |P|^2 + |A|^2 - 2 PВ·A. But |P|^2 = X^2 + p^2. And |A|^2 = r1^2. PВ·A = -r1 X. So

R^2 = X^2 + p^2 + r1^2 + 2 r1 X.

But also we have an expression from |P C|^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2. That's |v|^2? Actually |P C|^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2. And since |P A| = |P C|, we have R^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2. So

R^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2 = X^2 + 2 X r1 + r1^2 + p^2.

Thus R^2 = X^2 + p^2 + r1^2 + 2 r1 X. That's the same as above. So it's consistent. So R^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2.

Now, Оұ = r1 S / R^2. So Оұ = 1 if and only if R^2 = r1 S. Is that always true? Let's check numeric: r1=1, r2=1.5, R^2 вүҲ 3.5, r1 S = 1 * 3.5 = 3.5. Yes. r1=1, r2=1.2, R^2 вүҲ 3.2, r1 S = 3.2. Yes. r1=1, r2=1.8, R^2 вүҲ 3.8, r1 S = 3.8. So it seems that R^2 = r1 S. Let's verify analytically. We have R^2 = (X + r1)^2 + p^2. And we derived p^2 = \frac{ S^2 (1 - a^2)^2 }{16 y0^2 }. And also we have relation p y0 = -X (r1 + x0). That's not obviously leading to R^2 = r1 S. But maybe we can compute R^2 - r1 S using the expressions. Since we have R^2 expressed as (S/2)^2 + p^2. Now, what is r1 S? r1 S = r1 (1 + r1 + r2). That's something like r1 + r1^2 + r1 r2. We can try to express (X + r1) in terms of r1,r2. X = (1 + r2 - r1)/2. So X + r1 = (1 + r2 - r1 + 2 r1)/2 = (1 + r2 + r1)/2 = S/2. So that's nice. So R^2 = (S/2)^2 + p^2. So R^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2.

Now, r1 S = r1 (1 + r1 + r2). Is it equal to \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2? That would be a relation. Let's test with numeric: r1=1, r2=1.5 => S=3.5, S^2/4=3.0625, p^2вүҲ0.4378, sumвүҲ3.5. r1 S=3.5. Then \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} \left( 1 + \frac{ (1 - a^2)^2 }{4 y0^2 } \right). So the equation becomes:

\frac{S^2}{4} \left( 1 + \frac{ (1 - a^2)^2 }{4 y0^2 } \right) = r1 S.

Divide both sides by S (S>0): \frac{S}{4} \left( 1 + \frac{ (1 - a^2)^2 }{4 y0^2 } \right) = r1.

Thus r1 = \frac{S}{4} + \frac{S (1 - a^2)^2 }{16 y0^2 }.

But we can also compute r1 in terms of y0, S, a? That seems plausible if we also have an expression for y0^2 in terms of r1,r2,a. That's not obviously simplifying. However we can also compute p^2 from the formula p = -X (r1 + x0)/ y0, and then compute \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2 - r1 S. Let's attempt to compute that expression using the expressions for x0, y0, X, etc. Maybe it simplifies to 0 identically.

Now, also r2 = r1 + a. So r2^2 = r1^2 + 2 a r1 + a^2. Then 1 + r1^2 - r2^2 = 1 + r1^2 - r1^2 - 2 a r1 - a^2 = 1 - 2 a r1 - a^2. So (1 + r1^2 - r2^2)^2 = (1 - 2 a r1 - a^2)^2.

Thus 4 y0^2 = 4 r1^2 - (1 - 2 a r1 - a^2)^2.

Now, also S = 1 + r1 + r2 = 1 + 2 r1 + a. So S/4 = (1 + 2 r1 + a)/4. That seems not directly related.

Maybe we can try to compute r1 S = r1 (1 + 2 r1 + a) = r1 + 2 r1^2 + a r1. And \frac{S^2}{4} = \frac{ (1 + 2 r1 + a)^2 }{4}. That is something like (1 + 2 r1 + a)^2 /4. Then p^2 is something. The sum might simplify to r1 S. Let's test with symbolic algebra: set r1 = 1, a = 0.5 вҶ’ S = 1 + 2*1 + 0.5 = 3.5. Then \frac{S^2}{4} = 3.0625. p^2 = (1 - a^2)^2 S^2 / (16 y0^2). y0^2 = r1^2 - x0^2 = 1 - (-0.125)^2? Actually x0 = -0.125, so y0^2 = 1 - 0.015625 = 0.984375. Then (1 - a^2)^2 = 0.5625. Then p^2 = 0.5625 * 12.25 / (16 * 0.984375) = 6.890625 / 15.75 = 0.4378. Sum = 3.5 = r1 S. So equality holds. That suggests that \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2 = r1 S is an identity given the definitions. Let's try to prove it.

## Solution
We are given two circles О© and О“ with centres M and N respectively, such that the radius of О© is less than the radius of О“. They intersect at two distinct points A and B. The line MN meets О© at C and О“ at D, so that C, M, N, D lie on MN in that order. Let P be the circumcentre of triangle ACD. The line AP meets О© again at E (E вү  A) and О“ again at F (F вү  A). Let H be the orthocentre of triangle PMN.

Prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to the circumcircle of triangle BEF.

---

### 1.  Coordinate normalisation
Place the line MN as the xвҖ‘axis. Let M = (0,0). Since the circles intersect, the distance MN is strictly between |r2вҲ’r1| and r1+r2. After a suitable similarity (translation, rotation, scaling) we may assume MN = 1. Then N = (1,0).  
Let the radii be r1 (for О©) and r2 (for О“) with r1 < r2. The circles intersect, hence there exist points A and B on both circles, symmetric with respect to the xвҖ‘axis. Choose the upper intersection as  

\[
A = (x_0,\; y_0),\qquad y_0>0,
\]  

then  

\[
B = (x_0,\; -y_0).
\]  

They satisfy  

\[
x_0^2 + y_0^2 = r_1^2,\qquad (x_0-1)^2 + y_0^2 = r_2^2.
\]  

Subtracting gives  

\[
x_0 = \frac{1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2}{2}. \tag{1}
\]  

---

### 2.  Points C and D
О© intersects the xвҖ‘axis at (Вұr1,0). The order C, M, N, D along MN forces C to be the left intersection, so  

\[
C = (-r_1,\;0).
\]  

Similarly, О“ intersects the xвҖ‘axis at (1 Вұ r2,0). The order M, N, D forces D to be the right intersection, thus  

\[
D = (1+r_2,\;0).
\]  

The midpoint of CD is  

\[
X = \frac{-r_1 + (1+r_2)}{2} = \frac{1 + r_2 - r_1}{2}.
\]  

---

### 3.  The circumcentre P of triangle ACD
Because C and D lie on the xвҖ‘axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is the vertical line x = X. Hence the circumcentre P has xвҖ‘coordinate X, say  

\[
P = (X,\;p),\qquad p\in\mathbb R.
\]  

The equality of distances PA = PC yields a linear equation. Compute  

\[
P\!\cdot\!(C-A)=0 \quad\text{(since }|A|=|C|=r_1\text{)}.
\]  

\[
C-A = (-r_1 - x_0,\; -y_0),\qquad P\!\cdot\!(C-A)=X(-r_1-x_0)+p(-y_0)=0,
\]  

so  

\[
X(r_1+x_0) + p\,y_0 = 0. \tag{2}
\]  

From (2) we obtain  

\[
p = -\frac{X\,(r_1+x_0)}{y_0}. \tag{3}
\]  

---

### 4.  The line AP and points E, F
Let  

\[
v = P - A = (X - x_0,\; p - y_0).
\]  

Then AP is the line with direction v. The second intersections are  

\[
E = A + \alpha\,v,\qquad F = A + \beta\,v,
\]  

where Оұ and ОІ are positive scalars determined by the fact that E вҲҲ О© and F вҲҲ О“.  

Since |A|ВІ = rвӮҒВІ, we have  

\[
|A + \alpha v|^2 = r_1^2 \;\Longrightarrow\; 2\alpha\,A\!\cdot\!v + \alpha^2|v|^2 = 0 \;\Longrightarrow\; \alpha = \frac{r_1 S}{|v|^2},
\]  

where we have used  

\[
A\!\cdot\!v = A\!\cdot\!(P-A) = A\!\cdot\!P - r_1^2.
\]  

Similarly, because F lies on О“, we have |FвҲ’N|ВІ = rвӮӮВІ. Expanding gives  

\[
2\beta\,(A-N)\!\cdot\!v + \beta^2|v|^2 = r_2^2 - |A-N|^2 \quad\text{(after some algebra)}.
\]  

But it is easier to use the param directly and the relation  

\[
|F - N|^2 = r_2^2.
\]  

Since F = A + ОІ v, we obtain  

\[
|A - N + \beta v|^2 = r_2^2.
\]  

Because |AвҲ’N|ВІ = rвӮӮВІ (A is an intersection point of О© and О“), this simplifies to  

\[
2\beta\,(A-N)\!\cdot\!v + \beta^2|v|^2 = 0 \;\Longrightarrow\; \beta = \frac{r_2 S}{|v|^2}.
\]  

(The derivation is shown in the remark below.)

Thus  

\[
\alpha = \frac{r_1 S}{|v|^2},\qquad \beta = \frac{r_2 S}{|v|^2},\qquad S = 1 + r_1 + r_2. \tag{4}
\]  

---

### 5.  A useful simplification
From (2) we have  

\[
p\,y_0 = -X\,(r_1+x_0). \tag{5}
\]  

Now compute  

\[
r_1 + x_0 = r_1 + \frac{1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2}{2} = \frac{2r_1 + 1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2}{2} = \frac{(r_1+1)^2 - r_2^2}{2}.
\]  

Using \(r_2^2 = (r_1 + a)^2\) with \(a = r_2 - r_1\) we obtain  

\[
r_1 + x_0 = \frac{(1 - a)(1 + r_1 + r_2)}{2} = \frac{(1 - a)S}{2}. \tag{6}
\]  

Similarly,  

\[
X = \frac{1 + r_2 - r_1}{2} = \frac{1 + a}{2}. \tag{7}
\]  

Hence  

\[
X\,(r_1 + x_0) = \frac{(1 + a)(1 - a)S}{4} = \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}. \tag{8}
\]  

Now (5) becomes  

\[
p\,y_0 = -\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}. \tag{9}
\]  

But note that (9) gives  

\[
p = -\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4\,y_0}. \tag{10}
\]  

---

### 6.  The orthocentre H of triangle PMN
Because M = (0,0) and N = (1,0) are on the xвҖ‘axis, the altitude from P is perpendicular to MN, therefore it is the vertical line through P, i.e. \(x = X\).  
Thus the orthocentre H has the same xвҖ‘coordinate as P, say  

\[
H = (X,\; y_H).
\]  

The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. The condition \((H - M)\perp (N - P)\) gives  

\[
H\!\cdot\!(N - P) = 0.
\]  

Since M is the origin, this simplifies to  

\[
X\,(1 - X) + y_H\,(-p) = 0 \;\Longrightarrow\; y_H = \frac{X\,(1 - X)}{p}. \tag{11}
\]  

Using (7) and (10) we compute  

\[
X(1 - X) = \frac{1 + a}{2}\cdot\frac{1 - a}{2} = \frac{1 - a^2}{4}.
\]  

Therefore  

\[
y_H = \frac{ \frac{1 - a^2}{4} }{ p } = \frac{1 - a^2}{4p}. \tag{12}
\]  

Now substitute the expression (10) for p:

\[
y_H = \frac{1 - a^2}{4} \cdot \frac{1}{p} = \frac{1 - a^2}{4} \cdot \frac{4\,y_0}{(1 - a^2)S} = \frac{y_0}{S}.
\]  

But careful: p is negative, so (12) gives a negative number, and we got positive after multiplication? Let's re-evaluate.

We have (11): y_H = X (1 - X) / p. X (1 - X) = (1 - a^2)/4. p is negative, so y_H is negative. The expression we derived after substituting p from (10) gives

y_H = \frac{ (1 - a^2)/4 }{ - (1 - a^2)S/(4 y_0) } = \frac{ (1 - a^2)/4 }{ - (1 - a^2)S/(4 y_0) } = \frac{ (1 - a^2)/4 }{ - (1 - a^2)S/(4 y_0) } = \frac{ (1 - a^2)/4 } \cdot \frac{4 y_0}{ - (1 - a^2)S } = \frac{ y_0 }{ - S } = - \frac{ y_0 }{ S }.

Thus y_H = - y_0 / S. Good. So H = (X, - y_0 / S). (13)

---

### 7.  The circumcircle of triangle BEF
We have B = (x_0, -y_0).  
E = A + Оұ v = A + Оұ (P - A) = (1 - Оұ) A + Оұ P.  
F = A + ОІ v = (1 - ОІ) A + ОІ P.

Because Оұ = r_1 S / |v|^2, and ОІ = r_2 S / |v|^2, and we already observed that |v|^2 = r_1 S. Let's prove this fact.

**Claim:** |v|^2 = r_1 S.

*Proof:*  

\[
|v|^2 = |P - A|^2 = |P|^2 + |A|^2 - 2 P\!\cdot\!A.
\]  

We know |A|^2 = r_1^2.  
Also P is the circumcentre of ACD, so |P - A| = |P - C|. But we can compute |P - C|^2 directly:  

\[
|P - C|^2 = (X + r_1)^2 + p^2.
\]  

Since |P - A| = |P - C|, we have  

\[
|v|^2 = (X + r_1)^2 + p^2.
\]  

Now X + r_1 = (1 + r_2 - r_1)/2 + r_1 = (1 + r_2 + r_1)/2 = S/2.  

Thus  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2.
\]  

But from (9) we have p y_0 = - (1 - a^2) S / 4. Squaring gives  

\[
p^2 y_0^2 = \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16}.
\]  

Also, from (1) we can compute 4 y_0^2 = 4 r_1^2 - (1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2)^2.  
However, we can avoid explicit y_0 by noticing that  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16 y_0^2}.
\]  

On the other hand, from (5) we have p y_0 = - X (r_1 + x_0). Using (6) and (7) we already expressed X (r_1 + x_0) = (1 - a^2) S / 4. So  

\[
p = -\frac{(1 - a^2) S}{4 y_0}.
\]  

Now compute  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16 y_0^2} = \frac{S^2}{4} \left( 1 + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2}{4 y_0^2} \right).
\]  

We need to show that this equals r_1 S. So we need  

\[
\frac{S}{4} \left( 1 + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2}{4 y_0^2} \right) = r_1.
\]  

Equivalently,  

\[
r_1 = \frac{S}{4} + \frac{S (1 - a^2)^2}{16 y_0^2}.
\]  

Now recall that y_0^2 = r_1^2 - x_0^2. And x_0 is given by (1). We can compute 4 y_0^2 as  

\[
4 y_0^2 = 4 r_1^2 - (1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2)^2.
\]  

Also, a = r_2 - r_1. Then 1 - a^2 = 1 - (r_2 - r_1)^2 = 1 - (r_1^2 + r_2^2 - 2 r_1 r_2) = 1 - r_1^2 - r_2^2 + 2 r_1 r_2.  

Now we use the relation that A is on О“:  

\[
(x_0 - 1)^2 + y_0^2 = r_2^2.
\]  

Expanding:  

\[
x_0^2 - 2 x_0 + 1 + y_0^2 = r_2^2.
\]  

But \(x_0^2 + y_0^2 = r_1^2\), so  

\[
r_1^2 - 2 x_0 + 1 = r_2^2 \;\Longrightarrow\; 2 x_0 = r_1^2 + 1 - r_2^2.
\]  

This is just (1) rearranged. So no new info.

Instead, we can compute |v|^2 directly using the coordinates of P and A and then simplify using the expressions we have. But there is a more elegant way:  

From (5) we have \(p\,y_0 = -X\,(r_1+x_0)\).  
Now compute \(X + r_1 = \frac{S}{2}\). So \(X = \frac{S}{2} - r_1\).  
Also, \(r_1 + x_0 = \frac{(1 - a)S}{2}\).  
Thus  

\[
p\,y_0 = -\frac{S}{2}(1 - a) \cdot \frac{S}{2}? Wait careful:  

\(X\,(r_1+x_0) = \left(\frac{S}{2} - r_1\right) \cdot \frac{(1 - a)S}{2} = \frac{S}{2} \cdot \frac{(1 - a)S}{2} - r_1 \cdot \frac{(1 - a)S}{2} = \frac{S^2(1 - a)}{4} - \frac{r_1 (1 - a) S}{2}\).  

That doesn't look like the earlier expression (8) which gave \(\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}\). But note that (8) was derived from the product \(X (r_1 + x_0)\) using the expressions for X and r1+x0 separately:  

\(X = \frac{1 + a}{2}\), \(r_1 + x_0 = \frac{(1 - a)S}{2}\). Then product is \(\frac{(1 + a)(1 - a)S}{4} = \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}\). That's correct. So indeed \(X (r_1 + x_0) = \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}\). Therefore  

\[
p\,y_0 = -\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}. \tag{9}
\]  

Now, we also have  

\[
|v|^2 = (X - x_0)^2 + (p - y_0)^2.
\]  

But it's easier to compute \(|v|^2\) from \(|P - C|^2 = (X + r_1)^2 + p^2\). Since \(|P - A| = |P - C|\), we have  

\[
|v|^2 = (X + r_1)^2 + p^2.
\]  

Now \((X + r_1)^2 = \left(\frac{S}{2}\right)^2\). So  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2.
\]  

Now we also have \(p^2 = \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16 y_0^2}\). So  

\[
|v|^2 = S^2 \left( \frac{1}{4} + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2}{16 y_0^2} \right). \tag{14}
\]  

Now, note that \(y_0^2 = r_1^2 - x_0^2\). Using (1) we can compute \(4 y_0^2\) in terms of r1, r2, and then simplify. But perhaps we can find a simpler relation:  

From (9) we have \(p\,y_0 = -\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4}\). Also, from (3) we can express \(p\) in terms of \(y_0\) and \(X\) and \(r_1 + x_0\). However, we can also compute \(|v|^2\) in a different way:  

\[
|v|^2 = |P - A|^2 = (X - x_0)^2 + (p - y_0)^2.
\]  

But we can also compute \((X - x_0)\) and \((p - y_0)\) in terms of known quantities. Let's try that.

We have  

\[
X - x_0 = \frac{1 + r_2 - r_1}{2} - \frac{1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2}{2} = \frac{ r_2 - r_1 - r_1^2 + r_2^2 }{2} = \frac{ (r_2 - r_1)(1 + r_1 + r_2) }{2} = \frac{a S}{2}.
\]  

Thus  

\[
(X - x_0)^2 = \frac{a^2 S^2}{4}. \tag{15}
\]  

Now compute \(p - y_0\). Using (3) and (9) we have  

\[
p - y_0 = -\frac{X (r_1 + x_0)}{y_0} - y_0 = -\frac{ \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4} }{ y_0 } - y_0 = -\frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4 y_0} - y_0.
\]  

Thus  

\[
(p - y_0)^2 = \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16 y_0^2} + \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4} + y_0^2. \tag{16}
\]  

Therefore  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{a^2 S^2}{4} + \frac{(1 - a^2)^2 S^2}{16 y_0^2} + \frac{(1 - a^2)S}{4} + y_0^2.
\]  

Now, this looks messy, but we suspect that \(|v|^2\) simplifies to \(r_1 S\). Let's try to verify algebraically.

Recall that \(a = r_2 - r_1\), and \(S = 1 + r_1 + r_2 = 1 + 2r_1 + a\).  
Also, \(r_1 S = r_1 + 2 r_1^2 + a r_1\).  

Now, we can attempt to compute \(|v|^2 - r_1 S\) and see if it is zero. But maybe we can avoid this by noticing that from (14) we have  

\[
|v|^2 = \frac{S^2}{4} + p^2,
\]  

and we also have an expression for \(p^2\) that involves \(y_0\). But we could also express \(y_0\) in terms of r1 and S and a. Since we have \(x_0\) from (1) and \(y_0^2 = r_1^2 - x_0^2\). Let's compute \(4 y_0^2\):

\[
4 y_0^2 = 4 r_1^2 - (1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2)^2.
\]  

Now \(1 + r_1^2 - r_2^2 = 1 + r_1^2 - (r_1 + a)^2 = 1 + r_1^2 - r_1^2 -
